in the transaction manager, accumulator or waiting for acknowledgment,\n252:         // wait until these are completed.\n253:         while (!forceClose && ((this.accumulator.hasUndrained() || this.client.inFlightRequestCount() > 0) || hasPendingTransactionalRequests())) {\n254:             try {\n255:                 runOnce();\n256:             } catch (Exception e) {\n257:                 log.error(\"Uncaught error in kafka producer I/O thread: \", e);\n258:             }\n259:         }\n260: \n261:         // Abort the transaction if any commit or abort didn't go through the transaction manager's queue\n262:         while (!forceClose && transactionManager != null && transactionManager.hasOngoingTransaction()) {\n263:             if (!transactionManager.isCompleting()) {\n264:                 log.info(\"Aborting incomplete transaction due to shutdown\");\n265:                 try {\n266:                     // It is possible for the transaction manager to throw errors when aborting. Catch these\n267:                     // so as not to interfere with the rest of the shutdown logic.\n268:                     transactionManager.beginAbort();\n269:                 } catch (Exception e) {\n270:                     log.error(\"Error in kafka producer I/O thread while aborting transaction when during closing: \", e);\n271:                     // Force close in case the transactionManager is in error states.\n272:                     forceClose = true;\n273:                 }\n274:             }\n275:             try {\n276:                 runOnce();\n277:             } catch (Exception e) {\n278:                 log.error(\"Uncaught error in kafka producer I/O thread: \", e);\n279:             }\n280:         }\n281: \n282:         if (forceClose) {\n283:             // We need to fail all the incomplete transactional requests and batches and wake up the threads waiting on\n284:             // the futures.\n285:             if (transactionManager != null) {\n286:                 log.debug(\"Aborting incomplete transactional requests due to forced shutdown\");\n287:                 transactionManager.close();\n288:             }\n289:             log.debug(\"Aborting incomplete batches due to forced shutdown\");\n290:             this.accumulator.abortIncompleteBatches();\n291:         }\n292:         try {\n293:             this.client.close();\n294:         } catch (Exception e) {\n295:             log.error(\"Failed to close network client\", e);\n296:         }\n297: \n298:         log.debug(\"Shutdown of Kafka producer I/O thread has completed.\");\n299:     }\n300: \n301:     /**\n302:      * Run a single iteration of sending\n303:      *\n304:      */\n305:     void runOnce() {\n306:         if (transactionManager != null) {\n307:             try {\n308:                 transactionManager.maybeResolveSequences();\n309: \n310:                 RuntimeException lastError = transactionManager.lastError();\n311: \n312:                 // do not continue sending if the transaction manager is in a failed state\n313:                 if (transactionManager.hasFatalError()) {\n314:                     if (lastError != null)\n315:                         maybeAbortBatches(lastError);\n316:                     client.poll(retryBackoffMs, time.milliseconds());\n317:                     return;\n318:                 }\n319: \n320:                 if (transactionManager.hasAbortableError() && shouldHandleAuthorizationError(lastError)) {\n321:                     return;\n322:                 }\n323: \n324:                 // Check whether we need a new producerId. If so, we will enqueue an InitProducerId\n325:                 // request which will be sent below\n326:                 transactionManager.bumpIdempotentEpochAndResetIdIfNeeded();\n327: \n328:                 if (maybeSendAndPollTransactionalRequest()) {\n329:                     return;\n330:                 }\n331:             } catch (AuthenticationException e) {\n332:                 // This is already logged as error, but propagated here to perform any clean ups.\n333:                 log.trace(\"Authentication exception while processing transactional request\", e);\n334:                 transactionManager.authenticationFailed(e);\n335:             }\n336:         }\n337: \n338:         long currentTimeMs = time.milliseconds();\n339:         long pollTimeout = sendProducerData(currentTimeMs);\n340:         client.poll(pollTimeout, currentTimeMs);\n341:     }\n342: \n343:     // We handle {@code TransactionalIdAuthorizationException} and {@code ClusterAuthorizationException} by first\n344:     // failing the inflight requests, then transition the state to UNINITIALIZED so that the user doesn't need to\n345:     // instantiate the producer again.\n346:     private boolean shouldHandleAuthorizationError(RuntimeException exception) {\n347:         if (exception instanceof TransactionalIdAuthorizationException ||\n348:                         exception instanceof ClusterAuthorizationException) {\n349:             transactionManager.failPendingRequests(new AuthenticationException(exception));\n350:             maybeAbortBatches(exception);\n351:             transactionManager.transitionToUninitialized(exception);\n352:             return true;\n353:         }\n354:         return false;\n355:     }\n356: \n357:     private long sendProducerData(long now) {\n358:         MetadataSnapshot metadataSnapshot = metadata.fetchMetadataSnapshot();\n359:         // get the list of partitions with data ready to send\n360:         RecordAccumulator.ReadyCheckResult result = this.accumulator.ready(metadataSnapshot, now);\n361: \n362:         // if there are any partitions whose leaders are not known yet, force metadata update\n363:         if (!result.unknownLeaderTopics.isEmpty()) {\n364:             // The set of topics with unknown leader contains topics with leader election pending as well as\n365:             // topics which may have expired. Add the topic again to metadata to ensure it is included\n366:             // and request metadata update, since there are messages to send to the topic.\n367:             for (String topic : result.unknownLeaderTopics)\n368:                 this.metadata.add(topic, now);\n369: \n370:             log.debug(\"Requesting metadata update due to unknown leader topics from the batched records: {}\",\n371:                 result.unknownLeaderTopics);\n372:             this.metadata.requestUpdate(false);\n373:         }\n374: \n375:         // remove any nodes we aren't ready to send to\n376:         Iterator<Node> iter = result.readyNodes.iterator();\n377:         long notReadyTimeout = Long.MAX_VALUE;\n378:         while (iter.hasNext()) {\n379:             Node node = iter.next();\n380:             if (!this.client.ready(node, now)) {\n381:                 // Update just the readyTimeMs of the latency stats, so that it moves forward\n382:                 // every time the batch is ready (then the difference between readyTimeMs and\n383:                 // drainTimeMs would represent how long data is waiting for the node).\n384:                 this.accumulator.updateNodeLatencyStats(node.id(), now, false);\n385:                 iter.remove();\n386:                 notReadyTimeout = Math.min(notReadyTimeout, this.client.pollDelayMs(node, now));\n387:             } else {\n388:                 // Update both readyTimeMs and drainTimeMs, this would \"reset\" the node\n389:                 // latency.\n390:                 this.accumulator.updateNodeLatencyStats(node.id(), now, true);\n391:             }\n392:         }\n393: \n394:         // create produce requests\n395:         Map<Integer, List<ProducerBatch>> batches = this.accumulator.drain(metadataSnapshot, result.readyNodes, this.maxRequestSize, now);\n396:         addToInflightBatches(batches);\n397:         if (guaranteeMessageOrder) {\n398:             // Mute all the partitions drained\n399:             for (List<ProducerBatch> batchList : batches.values()) {\n400:                 for (ProducerBatch batch : batchList)\n401:                     this.accumulator.mutePartition(batch.topicPartition);\n402:             }\n403:         }\n404: \n405:         accumulator.resetNextBatchExpiryTime();\n406:         List<ProducerBatch> expiredInflightBatches = getExpiredInflightBatches(now);\n407:         List<ProducerBatch> expiredBatches = this.accumulator.expiredBatches(now);\n408:         expiredBatches.addAll(expiredInflightBatches);\n409: \n410:         // Reset the producer id if an expired batch has previously been sent to the broker. Also update the metrics\n411:         // for expired batches. see the documentation of @TransactionState.resetIdempotentProducerId to understand why\n412:         // we need to reset the producer id here.\n413:         if (!expiredBatches.isEmpty())\n414:             log.trace(\"Expired {} batches in accumulator\", expiredBatches.size());\n415:         for (ProducerBatch expiredBatch : expiredBatches) {\n416:             String errorMessage = \"Expiring \" + expiredBatch.recordCount + \" record(s) for \" + expiredBatch.topicPartition\n417:                 + \":\" + (now - expiredBatch.createdMs) + \" ms has passed since batch creation\";\n418:             failBatch(expiredBatch, new TimeoutException(errorMessage), false);\n419:             if (transactionManager != null && expiredBatch.inRetry()) {\n420:                 // This ensures that no new batches are drained until the current in flight batches are fully resolved.\n421:                 transactionManager.markSequenceUnresolved(expiredBatch);\n422:             }\n423:         }\n424:         sensors.updateProduceRequestMetrics(batches);\n425: \n426:         // If we have any nodes that are ready to send + have sendable data, poll with 0 timeout so this can immediately\n427:         // loop and try sending more data. Otherwise, the timeout will be the smaller value between next batch expiry\n428:         // time, and the delay time for checking data availability. Note that the nodes may have data that isn't yet\n429:         // sendable due to lingering, backing off, etc. This specifically does not include nodes with sendable data\n430:         // that aren't ready to send since they would cause busy looping.\n431:         long pollTimeout = Math.min(result.nextReadyCheckDelayMs, notReadyTimeout);\n432:         pollTimeout = Math.min(pollTimeout, this.accumulator.nextExpiryTimeMs() - now);\n433:         pollTimeout = Math.max(pollTimeout, 0);\n434:         if (!result.readyNodes.isEmpty()) {\n435:             log.trace(\"Nodes with data ready to send: {}\", result.readyNodes);\n436:             // if some partitions are already ready to be sent, the select time would be 0;\n437:             // otherwise if some partition already has some data accumulated but not ready yet,\n438:             // the select time will be the time difference between now and its linger expiry time;\n439:             // otherwise the select time will be the time difference between now and the metadata expiry time;\n440:             pollTimeout = 0;\n441:         }\n442:         sendProduceRequests(batches, now);\n443:         return pollTimeout;\n444:     }\n445: \n446:     /**\n447:      * Returns true if a transactional request is sent or polled, or if a FindCoordinator request is enqueued\n448:      */\n449:     private boolean maybeSendAndPollTransactionalRequest() {\n450:         if (transactionManager.hasInFlightRequest()) {\n451:             // as long as there are outstanding transactional requests, we simply wait for them to return\n452:             client.poll(retryBackoffMs, time.milliseconds());\n453:             return true;\n454:         }\n455: \n456:         if (transactionManager.hasAbortableError()) {\n457:             accumulator.abortUndrainedBatches(transactionManager.lastError());\n458:         } else if (transactionManager.isAborting()) {\n459:             accumulator.abortUndrainedBatches(new TransactionAbortedException());\n460:         }\n461: \n462:         TransactionManager.TxnRequestHandler nextRequestHandler = transactionManager.nextRequest(accumulator.hasIncomplete());\n463:         if (nextRequestHandler == null)\n464:             return false;\n465: \n466:         AbstractRequest.Builder<?> requestBuilder = nextRequestHandler.requestBuilder();\n467:         Node targetNode = null;\n468:         try {\n469:             FindCoordinatorRequest.CoordinatorType coordinatorType = nextRequestHandler.coordinatorType();\n470:             targetNode = coordinatorType != null ?\n471:                     transactionManager.coordinator(coordinatorType) :\n472:                     client.leastLoadedNode(time.milliseconds()).node();\n473:             if (targetNode != null) {\n474:                 if (!awaitNodeReady(targetNode, coordinatorType)) {\n475:                     log.trace(\"Target node {} not ready within request timeout, will retry when node is ready.\", targetNode);\n476:                     maybeFindCoordinatorAndRetry(nextRequestHandler);\n477:                     return true;\n478:                 }\n479:             } else if (coordinatorType != null) {\n480:                 log.trace(\"Coordinator not known for {}, will retry {} after finding coordinator.\", coordinatorType, requestBuilder.apiKey());\n481:                 maybeFindCoordinatorAndRetry(nextRequestHandler);\n482:                 return true;\n483:             } else {\n484:                 log.trace(\"No nodes available to send requests, will poll and retry when until a node is ready.\");\n485:                 transactionManager.retry(nextRequestHandler);\n486:                 client.poll(retryBackoffMs, time.milliseconds());\n487:                 return true;\n488:             }\n489: \n490:             if (nextRequestHandler.isRetry())\n491:                 time.sleep(nextRequestHandler.retryBackoffMs());\n492: \n493:             long currentTimeMs = time.milliseconds();\n494:             ClientRequest clientRequest = client.newClientRequest(targetNode.idString(), requestBuilder, currentTimeMs,\n495:                 true, requestTimeoutMs, nextRequestHandler);\n496:             log.debug(\"Sending transactional request {} to node {} with correlation ID {}\", requestBuilder, targetNode, clientRequest.correlationId());\n497:             client.send(clientRequest, currentTimeMs);\n498:             transactionManager.setInFlightCorrelationId(clientRequest.correlationId());\n499:             client.poll(retryBackoffMs, time.milliseconds());\n500:             return true;\n501:         } catch (IOException e) {\n502:             log.debug(\"Disconnect from {} while trying to send request {}. Going \" +\n503:                     \"to back off and retry.\", targetNode, requestBuilder, e);\n504:             // We break here so that we pick up the FindCoordinator request immediately.\n505:             maybeFindCoordinatorAndRetry(nextRequestHandler);\n506:             return true;\n507:         }\n508:     }\n509: \n510:     private void maybeFindCoordinatorAndRetry(TransactionManager.TxnRequestHandler nextRequestHandler) {\n511:         if (nextRequestHandler.needsCoordinator()) {\n512:             transactionManager.lookupCoordinator(nextRequestHandler);\n513:         } else {\n514:             // For non-coordinator requests, sleep here to prevent a tight loop when no node is available\n515:             time.sleep(retryBackoffMs);\n516:             metadata.requestUpdate(false);\n517:         }\n518: \n519:         transactionManager.retry(nextRequestHandler);\n520:     }\n521: \n522:     private void maybeAbortBatches(RuntimeException exception) {\n523:         if (accumulator.hasIncomplete()) {\n524:             log.error(\"Aborting producer batches due to fatal error\", exception);\n525:             accumulator.abortBatches(exception);\n526:         }\n527:     }\n528: \n529:     /**\n530:      * Start closing the sender (won't actually complete until all data is sent out)\n531:      */\n532:     public void initiateClose() {\n533:         // Ensure accumulator is closed first to guarantee that no more appends are accepted after\n534:         // breaking from the sender loop. Otherwise, we may miss some callbacks when shutting down.\n535:         this.accumulator.close();\n536:         this.running = false;\n537:         this.wakeup();\n538:     }\n539: \n540:     /**\n541:      * Closes the sender without sending out any pending messages.\n542:      */\n543:     public void forceClose() {\n544:         this.forceClose = true;\n545:         initiateClose();\n546:     }\n547: \n548:     public boolean isRunning() {\n549:         return running;\n550:     }\n551: \n552:     private boolean awaitNodeReady(Node node, FindCoordinatorRequest.CoordinatorType coordinatorType) throws IOException {\n553:         if (NetworkClientUtils.awaitReady(client, node, time, requestTimeoutMs)) {\n554:             if (coordinatorType == FindCoordinatorRequest.CoordinatorType.TRANSACTION) {\n555:                 // Indicate to the transaction manager that the coordinator is ready, allowing it to check ApiVersions\n556:                 // This allows us to bump transactional epochs even if the coordinator is temporarily unavailable at\n557:                 // the time when the abortable error is /**\n566:      * Handle a produce response\n567:      */\n568:     private void handleProduceResponse(ClientResponse response, Map<TopicPartition, ProducerBatch> batches, Map<Uuid, String> topicNames, long now) {\n569:         RequestHeader requestHeader = response.requestHeader();\n570:         int correlationId = requestHeader.correlationId();\n571:         if (response.wasTimedOut()) {\n572:             log.trace(\"Cancelled request with header {} due to the last request to node {} timed out\",\n573:                 requestHeader, response.destination());\n574:             for (ProducerBatch batch : batches.values())\n575:                 completeBatch(batch, new ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse(Errors.REQUEST_TIMED_OUT, String.format(\"Disconnected from node %s due to timeout\", response.destination())),\n576:                         correlationId, now, null);\n577:         } else if (response.wasDisconnected()) {\n578:             log.trace(\"Cancelled request with header {} due to node {} being disconnected\",\n579:                 requestHeader, response.destination());\n580:             for (ProducerBatch batch : batches.values())\n581:                 completeBatch(batch, new ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse(Errors.NETWORK_EXCEPTION, String.format(\"Disconnected from node %s\", response.destination())),\n582:                         correlationId, now, null);\n583:         } else if (response.versionMismatch() != null) {\n584:             log.warn(\"Cancelled request {} due to a version mismatch with node {}\",\n585:                     response, response.destination(), response.versionMismatch());\n586:             for (ProducerBatch batch : batches.values())\n587:                 completeBatch(batch, new ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse(Errors.UNSUPPORTED_VERSION), correlationId, now, null);\n588:         } else {\n589:             log.trace(\"Received produce response from node {} with correlation id {}\", response.destination(), correlationId);\n590:             // if we have a response, parse it\n591:             if (response.hasResponse()) {\n592:                 // Sender should exercise PartitionProduceResponse rather than ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse\n593:                 // https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/KAFKA-10696\n594:                 ProduceResponse produceResponse = (ProduceResponse) response.responseBody();\n595:                 // This will be set by completeBatch.\n596:                 Map<TopicPartition, Metadata.LeaderIdAndEpoch> partitionsWithUpdatedLeaderInfo = new HashMap<>();\n597:                 produceResponse.data().responses().forEach(r -> r.partitionResponses().forEach(p -> {\n598:                     ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse partResp = new ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse(\n599:                             Errors.forCode(p.errorCode()),\n600:                             p.baseOffset(),\n601:                             p.logAppendTimeMs(),\n602:                             p.logStartOffset(),\n603:                             p.recordErrors()\n604:                                 .stream()\n605:                                 .map(e -> new ProduceResponse.RecordError(e.batchIndex(), e.batchIndexErrorMessage()))\n606:                                 .collect(Collectors.toList()),\n607:                             p.errorMessage(),\n608:                             p.currentLeader());\n609: \n610:                     // Version 13 drop topic name and add support to topic id.\n611:                     // We need to find batch based on topic id and partition index only as\n612:                     // topic name in the response will be empty.\n613:                     // For older versions, topic id is zero, and we will find the batch based on the topic name.\n614:                     TopicPartition tp = (!r.topicId().equals(Uuid.ZERO_UUID) && topicNames.containsKey(r.topicId())) ?\n615:                             new TopicPartition(topicNames.get(r.topicId()), p.index()) :\n616:                             new TopicPartition(r.name(), p.index());\n617: \n618:                     ProducerBatch batch = batches.get(tp);\n619:                     if (batch == null) {\n620:                         throw new IllegalStateException(\"Can't find batch created for topic id \" + r.topicId() +\n621:                                 \" topic name \" + r.name() + \" partition \" + p.index() + \" using \" + topicNames);\n622:                     }\n623:                     completeBatch(batch, partResp, correlationId, now, partitionsWithUpdatedLeaderInfo);\n624:                 }));\n625: \n626:                 if (!partitionsWithUpdatedLeaderInfo.isEmpty()) {\n627:                     List<Node> leaderNodes = produceResponse.data().nodeEndpoints().stream()\n628:                         .map(e -> new Node(e.nodeId(), e.host(), e.port(), e.rack()))\n629:                         .filter(e -> !e.equals(Node.noNode()))\n630:                         .collect(\n631:                             Collectors.toList());\n632:                     Set<TopicPartition> updatedPartitions = metadata.updatePartitionLeadership(partitionsWithUpdatedLeaderInfo, leaderNodes);\n633:                     if (log.isTraceEnabled()) {\n634:                         updatedPartitions.forEach(\n635:                             part -> log.debug(\"For {} leader was updated.\", part)\n636:                         );\n637:                     }\n638:                 }\n639: \n640:                 this.sensors.recordLatency(response.destination(), response.requestLatencyMs());\n641:             } else {\n642:                 // this is the acks = 0 case, just complete all requests\n643:                 for (ProducerBatch batch : batches.values()) {\n644:                     completeBatch(batch, new ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse(Errors.NONE), correlationId, now, null);\n645:                 }\n646:             }\n647:         }\n648:     }\n649: \n650:     /**\n651:      * Complete or retry the given batch of records.\n652:      *\n653:      * @param batch The record batch\n654:      * @param response The produce response\n655:      * @param correlationId The correlation id for the request\n656:      * @param now The current POSIX timestamp in milliseconds\n657:      * @param partitionsWithUpdatedLeaderInfo This will be populated with partitions that have updated leader info.\n658:      */\n659:     private void completeBatch(ProducerBatch batch, ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse response, long correlationId,\n660:                                long now, Map<TopicPartition, Metadata.LeaderIdAndEpoch> partitionsWithUpdatedLeaderInfo) {\n661:         Errors error = response.error;\n662: \n663:         if (error == Errors.MESSAGE_TOO_LARGE && batch.recordCount > 1 && !batch.isDone() &&\n664:                 (batch.magic() >= RecordBatch.MAGIC_VALUE_V2 || batch.isCompressed())) {\n665:             // If the batch is too large, we split the batch and send the split batches again. We do not decrement\n666:             // the retry attempts in this case.\n667:             log.warn(\n668:                 \"Got error produce response in correlation id {} on topic-partition {}, splitting and retrying ({} attempts left). Error: {}\",\n669:                 correlationId,\n670:                 batch.topicPartition,\n671:                 this.retries - batch.attempts(),\n672:                 formatErrMsg(response));\n673:             if (transactionManager != null)\n674:                 transactionManager.removeInFlightBatch(batch);\n675:             this.accumulator.splitAndReenqueue(batch);\n676:             maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n677:             this.sensors.recordBatchSplit();\n678:         } else if (error != Errors.NONE) {\n679:             if (canRetry(batch, response, now)) {\n680:                 log.warn(\n681:                     \"Got error produce response with correlation id {} on topic-partition {}, retrying ({} attempts left). Error: {}\",\n682:                     correlationId,\n683:                     batch.topicPartition,\n684:                     this.retries - batch.attempts() - 1,\n685:                     formatErrMsg(response));\n686:                 reenqueueBatch(batch, now);\n687:             } else if (error == Errors.DUPLICATE_SEQUENCE_NUMBER) {\n688:                 // If we have received a duplicate sequence error, it means that the sequence number has advanced beyond\n689:                 // the sequence of the current batch, and we haven't retained batch metadata on the broker to return\n690:                 // the correct offset and timestamp.\n691:                 //\n692:                 // The only thing we can do is to return success to the user and not return a valid offset and timestamp.\n693:                 completeBatch(batch, response);\n694:             } else {\n695:                 // tell the user the result of their request. We only adjust sequence numbers if the batch didn't exhaust\n696:                 // its retries -- if it did, we don't know whether the sequence number was accepted or not, and\n697:                 // thus it is not safe to reassign the sequence.\n698:                 failBatch(batch, response, batch.attempts() < this.retries);\n699:             }\n700:             if (error.exception() instanceof InvalidMetadataException) {\n701:                 if (error.exception() instanceof UnknownTopicOrPartitionException) {\n702:                     log.warn(\"Received unknown topic or partition error in produce request on partition {}. The \" +\n703:                             \"topic-partition may not exist or the user may not have Describe access to it\",\n704:                         batch.topicPartition);\n705:                 } else {\n706:                     log.warn(\"Received invalid metadata error in produce request on partition {} due to {} Going \" +\n707:                             \"to request metadata update now\", batch.topicPartition, error.exception(response.errorMessage).toString());\n708:                 }\n709:                 if (error.exception() instanceof NotLeaderOrFollowerException || error.exception() instanceof FencedLeaderEpochException) {\n710:                     log.debug(\"For {}, received error {}, with leaderIdAndEpoch {}\", batch.topicPartition, error, response.currentLeader);\n711:                     if (partitionsWithUpdatedLeaderInfo != null\n712:                         && (response.currentLeader.leaderId() != -1 && response.currentLeader.leaderEpoch() != -1)) {\n713:                         partitionsWithUpdatedLeaderInfo.put(batch.topicPartition, new Metadata.LeaderIdAndEpoch(\n714:                             Optional.of(response.currentLeader.leaderId()), Optional.of(response.currentLeader.leaderEpoch())));\n715:                     }\n716:                 }\n717:                 metadata.requestUpdate(false);\n718:             }\n719:         } else {\n720:             completeBatch(batch, response);\n721:         }\n722: \n723:         // Unmute the completed partition.\n724:         if (guaranteeMessageOrder)\n725:             this.accumulator.unmutePartition(batch.topicPartition);\n726:     }\n727: \n728:     /**\n729:      * Format the error from a {@link ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse} in a user-friendly string\n730:      * e.g \"NETWORK_EXCEPTION. Error Message: Disconnected from node 0\"\n731:      */\n732:     private String formatErrMsg(ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse response) {\n733:         String errorMessageSuffix = (response.errorMessage == null || response.errorMessage.isEmpty()) ?\n734:                 \"\" : String.format(\". Error Message: %s\", response.errorMessage);\n735:         return String.format(\"%s%s\", response.error, errorMessageSuffix);\n736:     }\n737: \n738:     private void reenqueueBatch(ProducerBatch batch, long currentTimeMs) {\n739:         this.accumulator.reenqueue(batch, currentTimeMs);\n740:         maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches(batch);\n741:         this.sensors.recordRetries(batch.topicPartition.topic(), batch.recordCount);\n742:     }\n743: \n744:     private void completeBatch(ProducerBatch batch, ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse response) {\n745:         if (transactionManager != null) {\n746:             transactionManager.handleCompletedBatch(batch, response);\n747:         }\n748: \n749:         if (batch.complete(response.baseOffset, response.logAppendTime)) {\n750:             maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n751:         }\n752:     }\n753: \n754:     private void failBatch(ProducerBatch batch,\n755:                            ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse response,\n756:                            boolean adjustSequenceNumbers) {\n757:         final RuntimeException topLevelException;\n758:         if (response.error == Errors.TOPIC_AUTHORIZATION_FAILED)\n759:             topLevelException = new TopicAuthorizationException(Collections.singleton(batch.topicPartition.topic()));\n760:         else if (response.error == Errors.CLUSTER_AUTHORIZATION_FAILED)\n761:             topLevelException = new ClusterAuthorizationException(\"The producer is not authorized to do idempotent sends\");\n762:         else\n763:             topLevelException = response.error.exception(response.errorMessage);\n764: \n765:         if (response.recordErrors == null || response.recordErrors.isEmpty()) {\n766:             failBatch(batch, topLevelException, adjustSequenceNumbers);\n767:         } else {\n768:             Map<Integer, RuntimeException> recordErrorMap = new HashMap<>(response.recordErrors.size());\n769:             for (ProduceResponse.RecordError recordError : response.recordErrors) {\n770:                 // The API leaves us with some awkwardness interpreting the errors in the response.\n771:                 // We cannot differentiate between different error cases (such as INVALID_TIMESTAMP)\n772:                 // from the single error code at the partition level, so instead we use INVALID_RECORD\n773:                 // for all failed records and rely on the message to distinguish the cases.\n774:                 final String errorMessage;\n775:                 if (recordError.message != null) {\n776:                     errorMessage = recordError.message;\n777:                 } else if (response.errorMessage != null) {\n778:                     errorMessage = response.errorMessage;\n779:                 } else {\n780:                     errorMessage = response.error.message();\n781:                 }\n782: \n783:                 // If the batch contained only a single record error, then we can unambiguously\n784:                 // use the exception type corresponding to the partition-level error code.\n785:                 if (response.recordErrors.size() == 1) {\n786:                     recordErrorMap.put(recordError.batchIndex, response.error.exception(errorMessage));\n787:                 } else {\n788:                     recordErrorMap.put(recordError.batchIndex, new InvalidRecordException(errorMessage));\n789:                 }\n790:             }\n791: \n792:             Function<Integer, RuntimeException> recordExceptions = batchIndex -> {\n793:                 RuntimeException exception = recordErrorMap.get(batchIndex);\n794:                 if (exception != null) {\n795:                     return exception;\n796:                 } else {\n797:                     // If the response contains record errors, then the records which failed validation\n798:                     // will be present in the response. To avoid confusion for the remaining records, we\n799:                     // return a generic exception.\n800:                     return new KafkaException(\"Failed to append record because it was part of a batch \" +\n801:                         \"which had one more more invalid records\");\n802:                 }\n803:             };\n804: \n805:             failBatch(batch, topLevelException, recordExceptions, adjustSequenceNumbers);\n806:         }\n807:     }\n808: \n809:     private void failBatch(\n810:         ProducerBatch batch,\n811:         RuntimeException topLevelException,\n812:         boolean adjustSequenceNumbers\n813:     ) {\n814:         failBatch(batch, topLevelException, batchIndex -> topLevelException, adjustSequenceNumbers);\n815:     }\n816: \n817:     private void failBatch(\n818:         ProducerBatch batch,\n819:         RuntimeException topLevelException,\n820:         Function<Integer, RuntimeException> recordExceptions,\n821:         boolean adjustSequenceNumbers\n822:     ) {\n823:         this.sensors.recordErrors(batch.topicPartition.topic(), batch.recordCount);\n824: \n825:         if (batch.completeExceptionally(topLevelException, recordExceptions)) {\n826:             if (transactionManager != null) {\n827:                 try {\n828:                     // This call can throw an exception in the rare case that there's an invalid state transition\n829:                     // attempted. Catch these so as not to interfere with the rest of the logic.\n830:                     transactionManager.handleFailedBatch(batch, topLevelException, adjustSequenceNumbers);\n831:                 } catch (Exception e) {\n832:                     log.debug(\"Encountered error when transaction manager was handling a failed batch\", e);\n833:                 }\n834:             }\n835:             maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n836:         }\n837:     }\n838: \n839:     /**\n840:      * We can retry a send if the error is transient and the number of attempts taken is fewer than the maximum allowed.\n841:      * We can also retry OutOfOrderSequence exceptions for future batches, since if the first batch has failed, the\n842:      * future batches are certain to fail with an OutOfOrderSequence exception.\n843:      */\n844:     private boolean canRetry(ProducerBatch batch, ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse response, long now) {\n845:         return !batch.hasReachedDeliveryTimeout(accumulator.getDeliveryTimeoutMs(), now) &&\n846:             batch.attempts() < this.retries &&\n847:             !batch.isDone() &&\n848:             (transactionManager == null ?\n849:                     response.error.exception() instanceof RetriableException :\n850:                     transactionManager.canRetry(response, batch));\n851:     }\n852: \n853:     /**\n854:      * Transfer the record batches into a list of produce requests on a per-node basis\n855:      */\n856:     private void sendProduceRequests(Map<Integer, List<ProducerBatch>> collated, long now) {\n857:         for (Map.Entry<Integer, List<ProducerBatch>> entry : collated.entrySet())\n858:             sendProduceRequest(now, entry.getKey(), acks, requestTimeoutMs, entry.getValue());\n859:     }\n860: \n861:     /**\n862:      * Create a produce request from the given record batches\n863:      */\n864:     private void sendProduceRequest(long now, int destination, short acks, int timeout, List<ProducerBatch> batches) {\n865:         if (batches.isEmpty())\n866:             return;\n867: \n868:         final Map<TopicPartition, ProducerBatch> recordsByPartition = new HashMap<>(batches.size());\n869:         Map<String, Uuid> topicIds = topicIdsForBatches(batches);\n870: \n871:         ProduceRequestData.TopicProduceDataCollection tpd = new ProduceRequestData.TopicProduceDataCollection();\n872:         for (ProducerBatch batch : batches) {\n873:             TopicPartition tp = batch.topicPartition;\n874:             MemoryRecords records = batch.records();\n875:             Uuid topicId = topicIds.get(tp.topic());\n876:             ProduceRequestData.TopicProduceData tpData = tpd.find(tp.topic(), topicId);\n877: \n878:             if (tpData == null) {\n879:                 tpData = new ProduceRequestData.TopicProduceData()\n880:                         .setTopicId(topicId).setName(tp.topic());\n881:                 tpd.add(tpData);\n882:             }\n883: \n884:             tpData.partitionData().add(new ProduceRequestData.PartitionProduceData()\n885:                     .setIndex(tp.partition())\n886:                     .setRecords(records));\n887:             recordsByPartition.put(tp, batch);\n888:         }\n889: \n890:         String transactionalId = null;\n891:         boolean useTransactionV1Version = false;\n892:         if (transactionManager != null && transactionManager.isTransactional()) {\n893:             transactionalId = transactionManager.transactionalId();\n894:             useTransactionV1Version = !transactionManager.isTransactionV2Enabled();\n895:         }\n896: \n897:         ProduceRequest.Builder requestBuilder = ProduceRequest.builder(\n898:                 new ProduceRequestData()\n899:                         .setAcks(acks)\n900:                         .setTimeoutMs(timeout)\n901:                         .setTransactionalId(transactionalId)\n902:                         .setTopicData(tpd),\n903:                 useTransactionV1Version\n904:         );\n905:         // Fetch topic names from metadata outside callback as topic ids may change during the callback\n906:         // for example if topic was recreated.\n907:         Map<Uuid, String> topicNames = metadata.topicNames();\n908: \n909:         RequestCompletionHandler callback = response -> handleProduceResponse(response, recordsByPartition, topicNames, time.milliseconds());\n910: \n911:         String nodeId = Integer.toString(destination);\n912:         ClientRequest clientRequest = client.newClientRequest(nodeId, requestBuilder, now, acks != 0,\n913:                 requestTimeoutMs, callback);\n914:         client.send(clientRequest, now);\n915:         log.trace(\"Sent produce request to {}: {}\", nodeId, requestBuilder);\n916:     }\n917: \n918:     private Map<String, Uuid> topicIdsForBatches(List<ProducerBatch> batches) {\n919:         return batches.stream()\n920:                 .collect(Collectors.toMap(\n921:                         b -> b.topicPartition.topic(),\n922:                         b -> metadata.topicIds().getOrDefault(b.topicPartition.topic(), accumulated);\n178:                             int got = (int) Math.min(size - accumulated, this.nonPooledAvailableMemory);\n179:                             this.nonPooledAvailableMemory -= got;\n180:                             accumulated += got;\n181:                         }\n182:                     }\n183:                     // Don't reclaim memory on throwable since nothing was thrown\n184:                     accumulated = 0;\n185:                 } finally {\n186:                     // When this loop was not able to successfully terminate don't loose available memory\n187:                     this.nonPooledAvailableMemory += accumulated;\n188:                     this.waiters.remove(moreMemory);\n189:                 }\n190:             }\n191:         } finally {\n192:             // signal any additional waiters if there is more memory left\n193:             // over for them\n194:             try {\n195:                 if (!(this.nonPooledAvailableMemory == 0 && this.free.isEmpty()) && !this.waiters.isEmpty())\n196:                     this.waiters.peekFirst().signal();\n197:             } finally {\n198:                 // Another finally... otherwise find bugs complains\n199:                 lock.unlock();\n200:             }\n201:         }\n202: \n203:         if (buffer == null)\n204:             return safeAllocateByteBuffer(size);\n205:         else\n206:             return buffer;\n207:     }\n208: \n209:     // Protected for testing\n210:     protected void recordWaitTime(long timeNs) {\n211:         this.waitTime.record(timeNs, time.milliseconds());\n212:     }\n213: \n214:     /**\n215:      * Allocate a buffer.  If buffer allocation fails (e.g. because of OOM) then return the size count back to\n216:      * available memory and signal the next waiter if it exists.\n217:      */\n218:     private ByteBuffer safeAllocateByteBuffer(int size) {\n219:         boolean error = true;\n220:         try {\n221:             ByteBuffer buffer = allocateByteBuffer(size);\n222:             error = false;\n223:             return buffer;\n224:         } finally {\n225:             if (error) {\n226:                 this.lock.lock();\n227:                 try {\n228:                     this.nonPooledAvailableMemory += size;\n229:                     if (!this.waiters.isEmpty())\n230:                         this.waiters.peekFirst().signal();\n231:                 } finally {\n232:                     this.lock.unlock();\n233:                 }\n234:             }\n235:         }\n236:     }\n237: \n238:     // Protected for testing.\n239:     protected ByteBuffer allocateByteBuffer(int size) {\n240:         return ByteBuffer.allocate(size);\n241:     }\n242: \n243:     /**\n244:      * Attempt to ensure we have at least the requested number of bytes of memory for allocation by deallocating pooled\n245:      * buffers (if needed)\n246:      */\n247:     private void freeUp(int size) {\n248:         while (!this.free.isEmpty() && this.nonPooledAvailableMemory < size)\n249:             this.nonPooledAvailableMemory += this.free.pollLast().capacity();\n250:     }\n251: \n252:     /**\n253:      * Return buffers to the pool. If they are of the poolable size add them to the free list, otherwise just mark the\n254:      * memory as free.\n255:      *\n256:      * @param buffer The buffer to return\n257:      * @param size The size of the buffer to mark as deallocated, note that this may be smaller than buffer.capacity\n258:      *             since the buffer may re-allocate itself during in-place compression\n259: }\n275:     }\n276: \n277:     public void deallocate(ByteBuffer buffer) {\n278:         if (buffer != null)\n279:             deallocate(buffer, buffer.capacity());\n280:     }\n281: \n282: Final state, once set, is immutable. This function may be called\n242:      * once or twice on a batch. It may be called twice if\n243:      * 1. An inflight batch expires before a response from the broker is received. The batch's final\n244:      * state is set to FAILED. But it could succeed on the broker and second time around batch.done() may\n245:      * try to set SUCCEEDED final state.\n246:      * 2. If a transaction abortion happens or if the producer is closed forcefully, the final state is\n247:      * ABORTED but again it could succeed if broker responds with a success.\n248:      *\n249:      * Attempted transitions from [FAILED | ABORTED] --> SUCCEEDED are logged.\n250:      * Attempted transitions from one failure state to the same or a different failed state are ignored.\n251:      * Attempted transitions from SUCCEEDED to the same or a failed state throw an exception.\n252:      *\n253:      * @param baseOffset The base offset of the messages assigned by the server\n254:      * @param logAppendTime The log append time or -1 if CreateTime is being used\n255:      * @param topLevelException The exception that occurred (or null if the request was successful)\n256:      * @param recordExceptions Record exception function mapping batchIndex to the respective record exception\n257:      * @return true if the batch was completed successfully and false if the batch was previously aborted\n258:      */\n259:     private boolean done(\n260:         long baseOffset,\n261:         long logAppendTime,\n262:         RuntimeException topLevelException,\n263:         Function<Integer, RuntimeException> recordExceptions\n264:     ) {\n265:         final FinalState tryFinalState = (topLevelException == null) ? The distinction matters: `drain()` returns newly created batches being sent for the first time, while `getExpiredInflightBatches()` retrieves previously sent batches that have timed out. Looking at the sequence—line 395 drains fresh batches and adds them to in-flight tracking, then line 406 separately retrieves expired batches from earlier drains that have now exceeded their timeout window.\n\nThe race condition emerges when a batch times out while still being serialized. A batch gets added to in-flight tracking, begins its network write, and before that write completes, the batch's expiration timer triggers. This causes the pooled buffer to be returned and potentially reallocated to another batch, even though the original batch's data is still being transmitted.\n\nThe vulnerability lies in how `MemoryRecords` wraps the underlying `ByteBuffer` dynamically through `recordsBuilder.build()`. If the buffer gets deallocated during serialization, the write operation continues using freed memory that may now belong to a different batch.\n\nIn `sendProduceRequest()`, the records are obtained at line 874, then packaged into a `ProduceRequest` and sent via `client.send()`. However, there's no mechanism preventing a batch from expiring and freeing its buffer while the request is still being serialized to the network. The expiration path calls `failBatch()` to deallocate, but this happens independently of the sending operation, creating a race condition where serialization can write to already-freed memory. .records() to build the request, then at line 912-914 client.send() queues it for later serialization. Meanwhile, if the batch expires before serialization completes, the buffer gets deallocated and recycled to a new batch. When the network layer finally serializes the queued request, it's reading from a buffer that's now owned by a different batch—classic use-after-free.\n\nThe solution is to keep the buffer alive until serialization finishes, not just until the request object is created. At line 874, `batch.records()` is called which returns a MemoryRecords object\n2. This MemoryRecords holds a reference to the underlying buffer\n3. The MemoryRecords is added to the ProduceRequestData at line 886\n4. The ProduceRequest.Builder is created at line 897\n5. The ClientRequest is created at line 912 \n6. The request is sent at line 914The key question is: when does the serialization actually happen? If it happens during `client.send()` or later, then the buffer could be deallocated before serialization completes.\n\nNow let me look at the batch completion flow. In completeBatch() at line 744-751, I see that if the batch is complete, it calls `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch)` which deallocates immediately.\n\nBut wait, let me look more carefully at the race. In sendProducerData():\n- Line 395: drain() returns batches\n- Line 396: addToInflightBatches(batches)\n- Line 442: sendProduceRequests(batches)- These batches are the ones just drained\n\nThen at line 406-408:\n- getExpiredInflightBatches() looks in inFlightBatches\n- But the batches just added at line 396 would only be marked as expired if they have been in-flight long enough\n\nActually, I think the issue might be different. Let me look at how batches move through the system:\n\n1. Records are appended to accumulator\n2. accumulator.drain() removes ready batches and adds them to a list\n3. These batches are added to inFlightBatches\n4. sendProduceRequests() is called to send them\n5. Eventually the response comes back and the batch is completed/failed\n\nThe issue might be that:- In drain(), batches are removed from the accumulator's queue\n\n\n- When drain() returns, they're not yet tracked in inFlightBatches, so if expiration happens during the window between drain() and addToInflightBatches(), the batch won't be found by getExpiredInflightBatches(). Once they're added to inFlightBatches at line 396, expiration can trigger deallocation while the batch is still being serialized and sent.\n\nThe actual problem emerges during sendProduceRequest(): when batch.records() is called, it creates a MemoryRecords wrapper around the batch's ByteBuffer. This request gets queued via client.send(), but serialization happens later. If the batch expires and gets deallocated before serialization completes, the underlying ByteBuffer becomes invalid while the MemoryRecords still references it.\n\nThe sequence is: batch drains → sendProduceRequest queues the request → batch expires and buffer returns to the pool → new batch reuses that same memory → network layer tries to serialize the original request against now-corrupted data.\n\nTo prevent this, I need to either hold a reference to the batch until the response arrives, or copy the buffer contents into the request itself.\n\nLooking at MemoryRecords more closely, it seems to just reference the underlying buffer without owning it. The real issue surfaces when serializing the ProduceRequest—if the buffer has been recycled, the partition headers get mixed with message data from a different batch, causing messages to appear under the wrong topic. The fix requires ensuring the buffer stays allocated throughout the entire send cycle, not just until the batch But then sent again at line 442?\n\nNo, that doesn't make sense because batches from a previous drain would have been sent already.\n\nLet me think about this differently. The race condition description says:\n\"when an in-flight `ProducerBatch` expires or its broker disconnects, the batch's pooled `ByteBuffer` is returned to the `BufferPool` and immediately reused by a new batch — while the original batch's request is still being written to the network by the `Sender` thread.\"\n\nThis suggests:\n1. MEANWHILE, another event happens that causes Batch A to expire/fail\n6. failBatch() is called and deallocates Batch A's buffer\n7. The buffer is returned to pool and reused by Batch B\n8. The network layer tries to serialize Batch A's request but the buffer is now owned by Batch B\n\nThe key is that client.send() might queue the request asynchronously. Let me look for where the actual serialization happens...\n\n\nThe critical insight is that sendProduceRequest() could still be executing when the batch expires. If the batch's buffer gets deallocated and reused while sendProduceRequest() is still running, the serialization would write to a buffer now owned by another batch, corrupting its data.\n\nLooking at the flow: drain() retrieves batches, they're added to inflight tracking, expired batches are processed separately, then sendProduceRequests() executes. The vulnerability appears when a batch from the drain() call is simultaneously being expired—its buffer could be returned to the pool and immediately reallocated to a new batch before the original batch finishes writing to the network.\n\nThe sender thread operates sequentially, so the issue likely stems from async callbacks or response handling. In handleProduceResponse(), batches are completed and deallocated while their serialization might still be in progress. The problem is that batches can be added to inFlightBatches and then immediately checked for expiration before the send completes, creating a race condition where a batch's buffer gets deallocated while it's still being serialized. trying to serialize the request for batch A, but the buffer has already been deallocated and returned to the pool.\n\nActually, the Sender runs single-threaded, so this wouldn't happen across iterations. Let me reconsider the timing: sendProduceRequest() creates a ProduceRequest with MemoryRecords that reference the batch's buffer, then client.send() queues it. The actual serialization occurs during client.poll(), which happens after sendProducerData() completes. This means the buffer could be deallocated while the request sits queued but not yet serialized.\n\nWhen client.poll() eventually tries to serialize that queued request, the buffer is gone. Looking at the code flow around line 340, sendProducerData() returns first, then client.poll() is invoked. If sendProducerData() deallocates a batch that was just queued by sendProduceRequests(), the serialization will fail because the underlying buffer is invalid. The sequence is: sendProduceRequests() queues requests referencing batch buffers, sendProducerData() continues and deallocates expired batches, and if a queued batch happens to be expired, it gets freed before client.poll() can serialize it.\n\nHowever, expired batches are actually processed before sendProduceRequests() runs, so a freshly drained batch shouldn't be expired yet. The issue appears to involve re-enqueued batches. When a batch fails and gets re-enqueued back into the accumulator, it can end up in both the fresh batches list and the inFlightBatches map simultaneously. Each partition entry holds the partition index and Records buffer. If the MemoryRecords buffer gets reused across batches for different topics, the serialized request could end up with records from the wrong topic while the topic name field still references the original topic, creating a mismatch between what's in the records and what topic they're labeled as. When a buffer is deallocated, it's cleared and returned to the free pool. If that same buffer gets allocated to a new batch before the old batch finishes serializing, the serialization writes will overwrite the new batch's data. This could happen if batch A's serialization is delayed while batch B reuses the same buffer—the write operations intended for batch A end up corrupting batch B's contents instead. The broker would write to whichever topic the request header specifies, so if the header says topic=A but the buffer contains topic=B's records, they'd end up on topic A instead. That doesn't match the symptom though—the records are appearing on topic B. When serialization happens, it reads from the now-corrupted buffer containing Batch B's data, but the request header still says topic=A. The broker then writes those records to topic A based on the header, but they're actually Batch B's messages. So when reading from topic A, Batch B's data shows up there instead.\n\nThe symptom of messages appearing on the wrong topic could mean the request header points to one topic while the actual record contents belong to another—the broker follows the header and writes to the wrong destination, causing cross-topic message leakage.\n\nI think the core issue is a race condition where a batch's buffer gets deallocated while the request is still in flight. By that point the memory has been reused for different data. The fix would involve keeping the buffer alive until the request completes, likely by deferring deallocation until after the response is received.\n\nLooking at the actual code flow, failBatch() deallocates expired batches at line 418, which happens before sendProduceRequests() at line 442. For instance, Request A might have a topic A header but reference a buffer that's now filled with topic B's data. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01PXNUzcRpnfrZf8RUHAELSQ","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01JZ8qTigJ8jHwMWh7fJ1RRX","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/solution.md","content":"# Kafka Producer Buffer Pool Reuse Race Condition - Root Cause Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java` — Entry point with `sendProducerData()` and `failBatch()` methods; buffer lifecycle and batch deallocation\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/BufferPool.java` — Memory pool that manages buffer allocation and reuse; `deallocate()` returns buffers to free list\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/ProducerBatch.java` — Batch class with buffer reference; `records()` method returns MemoryRecords wrapping underlying ByteBuffer\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java` — Accumulator that holds batches; `deallocate()` method returns batch buffers to pool\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Symptom observed in**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 357-444)\n   - Messages occasionally appear on wrong topic due to corrupted produce request containing data from different batch\n\n2. **Called from**: `Sender.runOnce()` (line 305-341)\n   - Main sender loop calls `sendProducerData()` and then `client.poll()`\n\n3. **Buffer lifecycle initiated**: `Sender.sendProduceRequest()` (line 864-916)\n   - Line 874: `MemoryRecords records = batch.records()` — Returns MemoryRecords wrapping batch's ByteBuffer\n   - Line 884-886: MemoryRecords embedded in ProduceRequestData\n   - Line 912-914: ClientRequest created and `client.send()` queues request (NOT immediately serialized)\n\n4. **Buffer deallocation triggered**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 406-423)\n   - Line 406: `getExpiredInflightBatches()` finds in-flight batches that have timed out\n   - Line 418: `failBatch()` called for expired batches\n\n5. **Bug triggered by**: `Sender.failBatch()` (line 754-836)\n   - Line 825: `batch.completeExceptionally()` marks batch as failed\n   - **Line 835: `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch)` deallocates buffer unconditionally**\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`\n**Function**: `failBatch()` (overloaded at lines 754-815, 809-815, 817-836)\n**Line**: ~835 in `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch)` call within failBatch\n\n### Explanation\n\nThe race condition occurs when an in-flight ProducerBatch expires while its queued network request is still pending:\n\n1. **Phase 1 - Request Queued**:\n   - `sendProduceRequest()` (line 874) calls `batch.records()` which returns a `MemoryRecords` object that wraps the batch's underlying `ByteBuffer`\n   - This `MemoryRecords` is embedded in the `ProduceRequestData`\n   - `client.send()` (line 914) queues the request for later serialization\n\n2. **Phase 2 - Request Still Pending**:\n   - The request is queued but NOT immediately serialized (serialization happens during later `client.poll()`)\n   - Control returns from `sendProduceRequest()` to `sendProducerData()`\n\n3. **Phase 3 - Batch Expires**:\n   - While the request is still pending, `getExpiredInflightBatches()` (line 406) detects that the batch has exceeded its delivery timeout\n   - `failBatch()` is called at line 418\n   - At line 835, `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch)` deallocates the batch's buffer without checking if a request is still pending\n   - The buffer is returned to `BufferPool` via `free.deallocate(batch.buffer(), batch.initialCapacity())` (RecordAccumulator line 1032)\n\n4. **Phase 4 - Buffer Reused**:\n   - Another `ProducerBatch` for a different topic is allocated and receives the same pooled buffer (now cleared and available)\n   - Records for the new batch are written to this buffer\n\n5. **Phase 5 - Serialization Corruption**:\n   - `client.poll()` (line 340) attempts to serialize the originally queued request\n   - The request's `ProduceRequestData` contains `MemoryRecords` that reference the now-deallocated buffer\n   - The buffer now contains data from the NEW batch (different topic)\n   - The serialized request sends the new batch's message data but with the original batch's topic header\n   - Result: Messages for topic B are written with a request header indicating topic A (or vice versa)\n\n### Why This Occurs\n\nThe fundamental issue is **asynchronous request queueing without preventing buffer deallocation**:\n\n- `client.send()` queues requests without immediately serializing them\n- `failBatch()` deallocates batches without checking if they have pending requests in the queue\n- The sender thread has no mechanism to track which buffers are referenced by pending requests\n- Once deallocated, buffers are immediately available for reuse, creating a use-after-free race\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n### Option 1: Prevent Deallocation During Request Pending (Recommended)\n\n```diff\nprivate void failBatch(\n    ProducerBatch batch,\n    RuntimeException topLevelException,\n    Function<Integer, RuntimeException> recordExceptions,\n    boolean adjustSequenceNumbers\n) {\n    this.sensors.recordErrors(batch.topicPartition.topic(), batch.recordCount);\n\n    if (batch.completeExceptionally(topLevelException, recordExceptions)) {\n        if (transactionManager != null) {\n            try {\n                transactionManager.handleFailedBatch(batch, topLevelException, adjustSequenceNumbers);\n            } catch (Exception e) {\n                log.debug(\"Encountered error when transaction manager was handling a failed batch\", e);\n            }\n        }\n-       maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n+       // Only deallocate if the batch is not in-flight (no pending request)\n+       // If it's in-flight, the request may still be queued for serialization\n+       List<ProducerBatch> inflightBatches = inFlightBatches.get(batch.topicPartition);\n+       if (inflightBatches != null && inflightBatches.remove(batch)) {\n+           if (inflightBatches.isEmpty()) {\n+               inFlightBatches.remove(batch.topicPartition);\n+           }\n+           // Batch was removed from in-flight, but DO NOT deallocate yet\n+           // The pending request still references this batch's buffer\n+       } else {\n+           // Batch was not in-flight (no pending request), safe to deallocate\n+           maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches(batch);\n+           this.accumulator.deallocate(batch);\n+       }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Option 2: Defer Deallocation Until Response Callback\n\nModify `completeBatch()` to handle both successful and failed batches:\n\n```diff\nprivate void completeBatch(ProducerBatch batch, ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse response) {\n    if (transactionManager != null) {\n        transactionManager.handleCompletedBatch(batch, response);\n    }\n\n    if (batch.complete(response.baseOffset, response.logAppendTime)) {\n        maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n+   } else if (batch.isDone()) {\n+       // Batch was already marked failed (by failBatch), now deallocate after response\n+       maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n    }\n}\n```\n\nAnd modify `failBatch()` to skip deallocation:\n\n```diff\nprivate void failBatch(...) {\n    ...\n    if (batch.completeExceptionally(topLevelException, recordExceptions)) {\n        if (transactionManager != null) {\n            try {\n                transactionManager.handleFailedBatch(batch, topLevelException, adjustSequenceNumbers);\n            } catch (Exception e) {\n                log.debug(\"Encountered error when transaction manager was handling a failed batch\", e);\n            }\n        }\n-       maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n+       // Do NOT deallocate here - defer to response handler or explicit cleanup\n+       maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches(batch);\n+       // Deallocation happens in completeBatch when response is received, or in explicit timeout cleanup\n    }\n}\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Why Messages Appear on Wrong Topic\n\nThe produce request format includes:\n```\nProduceRequest {\n  TopicData {\n    Name: \"topic_A\"              ← Fixed in request header\n    PartitionData {\n      Index: 0                   ← Fixed\n      Records: MemoryRecords     ← References pooled ByteBuffer\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\nWhen the buffer is reused while serialization pending:\n\n1. Original request queued with: `topic_A, partition_0, buffer_X`\n2. Batch expires → buffer_X deallocated and returned to pool\n3. New batch for topic_B allocates and reuses buffer_X\n4. Records for topic_B written to buffer_X\n5. Request serializes as: `topic_A, partition_0, [data_from_topic_B]`\n6. Broker writes topic_B's records under topic_A partition_0\n7. Message appears on wrong topic or causes data corruption on broker\n\n### Root Cause Conditions Met\n\n✓ **Non-zero `linger.ms`** — Requests are queued and not immediately serialized\n✓ **Batch expiration during network latency** — Time window exists between queueing and serialization\n✓ **High message throughput** — New batches allocated quickly, reusing deallocated buffers\n✓ **Broker restarts/network issues** — Trigger batch expiration while requests pending\n\nThe CRC checksum passes because it only covers key/value/headers, not the topic header.\n\n### Why Existing Code Fails\n\nThe `inFlightBatches` tracking at line 396 (`addToInflightBatches(batches)`) documents which batches are pending requests, but this information is not checked in `failBatch()` before deallocation. Kafka Producer Buffer Pool Reuse Race Condition - Root Cause Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java` — Entry point with `sendProducerData()` and `failBatch()` methods; buffer lifecycle and batch deallocation\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/BufferPool.java` — Memory pool that manages buffer allocation and reuse; `deallocate()` returns buffers to free list\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/ProducerBatch.java` — Batch class with buffer reference; `records()` method returns MemoryRecords wrapping underlying ByteBuffer\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/RecordAccumulator.java` — Accumulator that holds batches; `deallocate()` method returns batch buffers to pool\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Symptom observed in**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 357-444)\n   - Messages occasionally appear on wrong topic due to corrupted produce request containing data from different batch\n\n2. **Called from**: `Sender.runOnce()` (line 305-341)\n   - Main sender loop calls `sendProducerData()` and then `client.poll()`\n\n3. **Buffer lifecycle initiated**: `Sender.sendProduceRequest()` (line 864-916)\n   - Line 874: `MemoryRecords records = batch.records()` — Returns MemoryRecords wrapping batch's ByteBuffer\n   - Line 884-886: MemoryRecords embedded in ProduceRequestData\n   - Line 912-914: ClientRequest created and `client.send()` queues request (NOT immediately serialized)\n\n4. **Buffer deallocation triggered**: `Sender.sendProducerData()` (line 406-423)\n   - Line 406: `getExpiredInflightBatches()` finds in-flight batches that have timed out\n   - Line 418: `failBatch()` called for expired batches\n\n5. **Bug triggered by**: `Sender.failBatch()` (line 754-836)\n   - Line 825: `batch.completeExceptionally()` marks batch as failed\n   - **Line 835: `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch)` deallocates buffer unconditionally**\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/internals/Sender.java`\n**Function**: `failBatch()` (overloaded at lines 754-815, 809-815, 817-836)\n**Line**: ~835 in `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch)` call within failBatch\n\n### Explanation\n\nThe race condition occurs when an in-flight ProducerBatch expires while its queued network request is still pending:\n\n1. **Phase 1 - Request Queued**:\n   - `sendProduceRequest()` (line 874) calls `batch.records()` which returns a `MemoryRecords` object that wraps the batch's underlying `ByteBuffer`\n   - This `MemoryRecords` is embedded in the `ProduceRequestData`\n   - `client.send()` (line 914) queues the request for later serialization\n\n2. **Phase 2 - Request Still Pending**:\n   - The request is queued but NOT immediately serialized (serialization happens during later `client.poll()`)\n   - Control returns from `sendProduceRequest()` to `sendProducerData()`\n\n3. **Phase 3 - Batch Expires**:\n   - While the request is still pending, `getExpiredInflightBatches()` (line 406) detects that the batch has exceeded its delivery timeout\n   - `failBatch()` is called at line 418\n   - At line 835, `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch)` deallocates the batch's buffer without checking if a request is still pending\n   - The buffer is returned to `BufferPool` via `free.deallocate(batch.buffer(), batch.initialCapacity())` (RecordAccumulator line 1032)\n\n4. **Phase 4 - Buffer Reused**:\n   - Another `ProducerBatch` for a different topic is allocated and receives the same pooled buffer (now cleared and available)\n   - Records for the new batch are written to this buffer\n\n5. **Phase 5 - Serialization Corruption**:\n   - `client.poll()` (line 340) attempts to serialize the originally queued request\n   - The request's `ProduceRequestData` contains `MemoryRecords` that reference the now-deallocated buffer\n   - The buffer now contains data from the NEW batch (different topic)\n   - The serialized request sends the new batch's message data but with the original batch's topic header\n   - Result: Messages for topic B are written with a request header indicating topic A (or vice versa)\n\n### Why This Occurs\n\nThe fundamental issue is **asynchronous request queueing without preventing buffer deallocation**:\n\n- `client.send()` queues requests without immediately serializing them\n- `failBatch()` deallocates batches without checking if they have pending requests in the queue\n- The sender thread has no mechanism to track which buffers are referenced by pending requests\n- Once deallocated, buffers are immediately available for reuse, creating a use-after-free race\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n### Option 1: Prevent Deallocation During Request Pending (Recommended)\n\n```diff\nprivate void failBatch(\n    ProducerBatch batch,\n    RuntimeException topLevelException,\n    Function<Integer, RuntimeException> recordExceptions,\n    boolean adjustSequenceNumbers\n) {\n    this.sensors.recordErrors(batch.topicPartition.topic(), batch.recordCount);\n\n    if (batch.completeExceptionally(topLevelException, recordExceptions)) {\n        if (transactionManager != null) {\n            try {\n                transactionManager.handleFailedBatch(batch, topLevelException, adjustSequenceNumbers);\n            } catch (Exception e) {\n                log.debug(\"Encountered error when transaction manager was handling a failed batch\", e);\n            }\n        }\n-       maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n+       // Only deallocate if the batch is not in-flight (no pending request)\n+       // If it's in-flight, the request may still be queued for serialization\n+       List<ProducerBatch> inflightBatches = inFlightBatches.get(batch.topicPartition);\n+       if (inflightBatches != null && inflightBatches.remove(batch)) {\n+           if (inflightBatches.isEmpty()) {\n+               inFlightBatches.remove(batch.topicPartition);\n+           }\n+           // Batch was removed from in-flight, but DO NOT deallocate yet\n+           // The pending request still references this batch's buffer\n+       } else {\n+           // Batch was not in-flight (no pending request), safe to deallocate\n+           maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches(batch);\n+           this.accumulator.deallocate(batch);\n+       }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Option 2: Defer Deallocation Until Response Callback\n\nModify `completeBatch()` to handle both successful and failed batches:\n\n```diff\nprivate void completeBatch(ProducerBatch batch, ProduceResponse.PartitionResponse response) {\n    if (transactionManager != null) {\n        transactionManager.handleCompletedBatch(batch, response);\n    }\n\n    if (batch.complete(response.baseOffset, response.logAppendTime)) {\n        maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n+   } else if (batch.isDone()) {\n+       // Batch was already marked failed (by failBatch), now deallocate after response\n+       maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n    }\n}\n```\n\nAnd modify `failBatch()` to skip deallocation:\n\n```diff\nprivate void failBatch(...) {\n    ...\n    if (batch.completeExceptionally(topLevelException, recordExceptions)) {\n        if (transactionManager != null) {\n            try {\n                transactionManager.handleFailedBatch(batch, topLevelException, adjustSequenceNumbers);\n            } catch (Exception e) {\n                log.debug(\"Encountered error when transaction manager was handling a failed batch\", e);\n            }\n        }\n-       maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);\n+       // Do NOT deallocate here - defer to response handler or explicit cleanup\n+       maybeRemoveFromInflightBatches(batch);\n+       // Deallocation happens in completeBatch when response is received, or in explicit timeout cleanup\n    }\n}\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Why Messages Appear on Wrong Topic\n\nThe produce request format includes:\n```\nProduceRequest {\n  TopicData {\n    Name: \"topic_A\"              ← Fixed in request header\n    PartitionData {\n      Index: 0                   ← Fixed\n      Records: MemoryRecords     ← References pooled ByteBuffer\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\nWhen the buffer is reused while serialization pending:\n\n1. Original request queued with: `topic_A, partition_0, buffer_X`\n2. Batch expires → buffer_X deallocated and returned to pool\n3. New batch for topic_B allocates and reuses buffer_X\n4. Records for topic_B written to buffer_X\n5. Request serializes as: `topic_A, partition_0, [data_from_topic_B]`\n6. Broker writes topic_B's records under topic_A partition_0\n7. Message appears on wrong topic or causes data corruption on broker\n\n### Root Cause Conditions Met\n\n✓ **Non-zero `linger.ms`** — Requests are queued and not immediately serialized\n✓ **Batch expiration during network latency** — Time window exists between queueing and serialization\n✓ **High message throughput** — New batches allocated quickly, reusing deallocated buffers\n✓ **Broker restarts/network issues** — Trigger batch expiration while requests pending\n\nThe CRC checksum passes because it only covers key/value/headers, not the topic header.\n\n### Why Existing Code Fails\n\nThe `inFlightBatches` tracking at line 396 (`addToInflightBatches(batches)`) documents which batches are pending requests, but this information is not checked in `failBatch()` before deallocation. The batch enters inFlightBatches, but can be deallocated before the request completes, violating the buffer lifecycle assumption.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
